Even so, I will never forget that feeling of innate fear “of the unknown” preceding our duties that night.
* [26 May 2019](https://web.archive.org/web/20210531020047/https://twitter.com/KosChertified/status/1132692409802842112): It was only weeks after painting that school house. I was tagged to fly the first mission of Desert Storm that night in January, 1991, topping off my tanks from a KC-135 so that I could later fuel the inbound Intruders before they went “feet dry”.
* [26 May 2019](https://web.archive.org/web/20210531020047/https://twitter.com/KosChertified/status/1132692409802842112): Of course we had our attention pinned to the the tiny television in the top corner of that space, watching CNN and wondering “when it would all begin?”
* [26 May 2019](https://web.archive.org/web/20210531020047/https://twitter.com/KosChertified/status/1132692409802842112): Back on cruise Tom & I were in separate quarters of the ship, segregated by aircraft squadrons, and so we didn’t run in to each other too often. It was mainly in the dirty shirt mess (where pilots can wear their bags), grabbing chow, that we’d bump into each other & have a chat.
* [26 May 2019](https://web.archive.org/web/20210531020047/https://twitter.com/KosChertified/status/1132692409802842112): He flew A-6 Intruders, something I kept off my “dreamsheet” in the selection process because they fly high speed “low level” missions - AT NIGHT! I didn’t have it in me to take those perilous risks every day as a regular job routine. But William “Tom” Costen had The Right Stuff!
* [26 May 2019](https://web.archive.org/web/20210531020047/https://twitter.com/KosChertified/status/1132692409802842112): Work side by side with someone for 12 hours in grueling humid heat and you’ll get to know them pretty well. Tom was a great guy!
* [26 May 2019](https://web.archive.org/web/20210531020047/https://twitter.com/KosChertified/status/1132692409802842112): We loaded pallets of paint on the stake truck, and with the help of our enlisted shipmates we all drove out to a public school house outside of town & spent the entire day making its exterior look vibrant & new. The school staff and students were most appreciative of our efforts.
* [26 May 2019](https://web.archive.org/web/20210531020047/https://twitter.com/KosChertified/status/1132692409802842112): I knew him as Tom Costen, but his given first name was William. We both had planned months ahead with the Ranger Chaplain’s office coordinating our Navy “Project Handclasp” charity work.   Then one early morning on our very first (hot) day at Subic Bay, P.I., it began. pic.twitter.com/SDUiogfZtp
* [25 May 2019](https://web.archive.org/web/20210530204128/https://twitter.com/KosChertified/status/1132292091625713671): “I think one measure of a man is those who stand with him at the end of his days. For us younger guys, we could only imagine what kind of commander it is that has admirals for pallbearers.”
* [25 May 2019](https://web.archive.org/web/20210530204128/https://twitter.com/KosChertified/status/1132292091625713671): We extend our appreciation to Capt William Shivell for authoring and recording these memories of a man who was a legend in his own time.🇺🇸
* [25 May 2019](https://web.archive.org/web/20210530204128/https://twitter.com/KosChertified/status/1132292091625713671): “As I recall, Bug's last words were ‘What a lousy day. Well, I gotta get out of here. I'll see you guys....’ His wingman, "Dude" Holden, never saw a good chute.”
* [25 May 2019](https://web.archive.org/web/20210530204128/https://twitter.com/KosChertified/status/1132292091625713671): A Lousy October Day (1991):  “A Bandit airborne had relayed that the engine in Bandit 31, an A-4E, had gone sour and the pilot was punching out. It was Bug. After several relight attempts, Bug knew he had to eject.”
* [25 May 2019](https://web.archive.org/web/20210530204128/https://twitter.com/KosChertified/status/1132292091625713671): ”He always had a word of encouragement in a debrief for the nugget who got his tail waxed in the air. And he always had time to share a story with that nugget over a beer, even though he always held court with those old guys we called skipper, CAG or admiral.”
* [25 May 2019](https://web.archive.org/web/20210530204128/https://twitter.com/KosChertified/status/1132292091625713671): “If you were a fighter pilot at Miramar...you couldn't help but see Bug in action, either at the merge or at the club. In either place, you found that Bug's talents in the air were equal only to his humility on the ground. He greeted everybody, old salt or nugget, with amity.”
* [25 May 2019](https://web.archive.org/web/20210530204128/https://twitter.com/KosChertified/status/1132292091625713671): CDR Roach was a veteran of 11 cruises in 23 years, accumulated over 5,000 hours of flight time in various fighter aircraft, over 1,000 carrier landings, and over 250 combat missions spanning two wars.
* [25 May 2019](https://web.archive.org/web/20210530204128/https://twitter.com/KosChertified/status/1132292091625713671): Recognizing CDR Roach's enormous contribution to naval aviation, the Northern California Coastal Navy League established the Commander John "Bug" Roach Paddles Award for LSO excellence.
* [25 May 2019](https://web.archive.org/web/20210530204128/https://twitter.com/KosChertified/status/1132292091625713671): CDR Roach was the Navy's senior LSO. He "waved" more aircraft than any other LSO in the Navy (over 130,000 landings).
* [25 May 2019](https://web.archive.org/web/20210530204128/https://twitter.com/KosChertified/status/1132292091625713671): Having been escorted by him in his F-14 Tomcat was a blessing, as Bug had 11 cruises & two wars under his belt.  If you can spare 20 minutes free from your TV this weekend, it would be time well spent if you read “Bug’s Life” and “Remembering Bug” found at  https://store.tailhook.net/b-bug-roach.html
* [25 May 2019](https://web.archive.org/web/20210530204128/https://twitter.com/KosChertified/status/1132292091625713671): CDR “Bug” Roach was no ordinary Naval Aviator. He was “larger than life”, California raised, but had a cowboy appearance with his pronounced un-Officer like mustache, steel-tipped cowboy boots with his flight suit and a large metal belt buckle spelling out “BUG”. pic.twitter.com/bKARdfY5xp
